[showed](https://www.facebook.com/kontra.daya/photos/a.341444269288445/1848189788613878/)
that their votes had been [tallied](http://www.votereportph.com/) [for
Duterte's
slate](https://www.facebook.com/frohniedipc/posts/10219325598039653)
instead]{.underline}. Some ballots allegedly
[omitted](https://www.facebook.com/kadamaynational/posts/830098934012274)
progressive party lists altogether, while viral social media posts
[falsely
claimed](https://www.facebook.com/PhilippineSTAR/photos/a.134754620011561/1344592452361099)
that these had been "disqualified" for "destabilizing the government."
**[U.S. support has been critical to the rise of Duterte's military and
police.]{.underline}** After publicly reporting 0.4 percent of
precincts' results, the election commission's servers suddenly [shut
down for seven
hours](https://www.rappler.com/nation/politics/elections/2019/230538-after-hours-long-glitch-comelec-transparency-server-sends-results-again).
When they went back online, over 90 percent of results were in,
proclaiming that Duterte's picks had won the Upper House. For his part,
[Duterte made a mockery of democracy,]{.underline} commenting that
vote-buying is
"[integral](https://l.facebook.com/l.php?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.rappler.com%2Fnation%2Fpolitics%2Felections%2F2019%2F230486-duterte-says-vote-buying-integral%3Ffbclid%3DIwAR3qQ3MOF5x6r6UOhRvgqjv6zmZFld1eBJMc_feUfTJCPz1w3NnkXcZJVE4&h=AT0itBfXWvS6uREx12D3AhSgMAsqB_Oek9XKyBFJjXf7npCBUMrSXcKc6L_H3_h1sAJyEssj9TXZRBJ1Jrl77R7G7xKPIVgV-XCU8xEPHpjq1PATIemE-4D42AjPzg)"
and "there's no one who doesn't buy votes." Then there's the
intimidation by the Philippine armed forces, who increasingly function
as Duterte's
[goons](https://www.hsfk.de/fileadmin/HSFK/hsfk_publikationen/prif142.pdf)
--- not only through his infamous "[drug
war](https://www.amnesty.org.uk/files/2017-04/ASA3555172017ENGLISH.PDF?),"
but during the elections too. [In Manila, [uniformed
police](https://www.bulatlat.com/2019/05/13/comelec-urged-to-probe-polices-partisan-activities/?fbclid=IwAR04I9AktBhqLWphGjI5tKS9CxrzXn-F0-93qbBsMxEuqv_LBtriC3FkYj4)
distributed propaganda newsletters maligning and red-baiting progressive
candidates, a McCarthy-era tactic used not only to intimidate, but to
target and [kill
activists](https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2019/01/philippines-peace-advocate-gunned-down-in-yet-another-targeted-killing/)]{.underline}.
Across the country, volunteers for the progressive Makabayan bloc
received [death
threats](https://www.bulatlat.com/2019/05/13/state-security-forces-resort-to-death-threats-red-tagging-against-makabayan-party-list-groups-supporters/?fbclid=IwAR35WQYzpKjBJAbUlwadM4vxSSyiLigRYbGFEesylK0JeEz0fDHpXg7Y9IU)
and voters were [intimidated through
misinformation](https://l.facebook.com/l.php?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bulatlat.com%2F2019%2F05%2F13%2Fstate-security-forces-resort-to-death-threats-red-tagging-against-makabayan-party-list-groups-supporters%2F%3Ffbclid%3DIwAR2BzNaxnAeVOXThDB4Lr5avw5hUxOC4FdPomV10V9ZbS38FGEKRny24p2o&h=AT3bPxoUW1Ff9HuFpSDcu1fuSRYTE79PAeEWqsnPYL1P6jybPDuPvm-ZFxQONsu4b1LDxwV5RaZOZua4TZtFuMsVtxNR0BzrB2w0euN-KS-fJgCvpUcZT5r8Wce6kg).
Overseas,
**[[millions](https://www.philstar.com/headlines/2019/05/01/1914073/migrante-claims-18-m-overseas-voters-disenfranchised)
of overseas Filipinos have been disenfranchised, and their votes left
uncounted.]{.underline}** One voter, Dominico Vega, who has been
organizing students at California State University Northridge to lobby
for a congressional hearing on the Philippines, expressed: "The
Philippines can feel so far from the San Fernando Valley, but when
friends and family become victims of Duterte's human rights abuses, it
hits close to home. Elections should not silence us." Vega is right in
his call for a congressional hearing on the Philippines: **[U.S. support
has been critical to
[the](https://www.philstar.com/opinion/2018/10/21/1861787/afp-budget-biggest-ever)
[rise](https://news.abs-cbn.com/news/01/09/18/cops-soldiers-other-uniformed-personnel-to-begin-receiving-doubled-pay)
[of](http://cnnphilippines.com/news/2018/08/30/DND-Defense-proposed-budget-2019.html)
Duterte's military and police. Duterte's regime is the
[largest](http://philippineslifestyle.com/military-aid-usa-philippines/)]{.underline}**
[**[recipient]{.underline}**](https://www.philstar.com/headlines/2018/09/10/1850124/philippines-largest-recipient-us-military-aid)
**[of U.S. military
[aid](https://explorer.usaid.gov/agencies/?agency=7&year=2017&measure=Obligations)
in East and Southeast Asia. In 2018, the U.S. sent [over \$193.5
million](https://fpif.org/its-time-to-end-u-s-military-aid-to-the-philippines/)
in military aid to the Philippine military and police, not including
[arms
sales](https://www.warresisters.org/sites/default/files/fy2020pie_chart-low_resb.pdf),
and donated equipment of unreported value.]{.underline}** The **[U.S.
helped inaugurate Duterte's drug war,]{.underline}** which has [now
claimed as many as
[27,000](https://news.abs-cbn.com/focus/12/05/18/chr-chief-drug-war-deaths-could-be-as-high-as-27000)
lives, by giving the police [\$32
million](http://www.philstar.com/headlines/2016/07/27/1607298/us-pledges-32m-philippine-law-enforcement)
for
[equipment](https://oig.usaid.gov/sites/default/files/2018-11/lig-oco-opep-0918.pdf)
and
[training](http://www.rappler.com/nation/147196-us-funding-philippines-law-enforcement)
in "policing standards]{.underline}" --- clearly detrimental when it
comes to human rights. Less publicized in the U.S., Duterte has imposed
martial law on the island of Mindanao since 2017. [Increased
militarization and bombings there, backed by U.S. drones, advisors, and
special forces, have caused the displacement of some
[450,000](https://www.karapatan.org/2018-Karapatan-HR-Report)
civilians.]{.underline} Philippine
[soldiers](http://iboninternational.org/sites/ibon/files/resources/DKC-booklet.pdf)
and
[paramilitaries](https://drive.google.com/file/d/1pTShcOkHjqndw19oeREZrCuGFneEXPts/view)
are meanwhile committing [atrocities against indigenous
communities]{.underline} who
[oppose](https://intercontinentalcry.org/thousands-march-killings-indigenous-peoples-philippine-mining-capital/)
the encroachments of logging and mining conglomerates. U.S. military
**[aid]{.underline}**, often through secretive and unaccountable
conduits in the name of the War on Terror, **[is only making this
internal conflict and the overall human rights crisis
worse.]{.underline}** U.S. military aid, often through
[secretive](https://fpif.org/its-time-to-end-u-s-military-aid-to-the-philippines/)
and [unaccountable](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/natsec/R44519.pdf) conduits
in the name of the War on Terror, is only making this internal conflict
and the overall human rights crisis worse. U.S. military aid does not
serve to defend the Philippines against invaders --- rather, [it is
being turned against the
[vulnerable](http://iboninternational.org/sites/ibon/files/resources/DKC-booklet.pdf)
and
[marginalized](https://drive.google.com/file/d/1Okck6AWGtYBxC2ZpqEfnFaOLYE1arKAT/view),
the
[journalists](https://newsinfo.inquirer.net/1013357/22-journalists-killed-in-ph-under-duterte-administration-nujp)
and [human
rights](https://www.rappler.com/newsbreak/iq/222796-human-rights-defenders-killed-under-duterte-administration)
defenders, the
[dissenters](https://www.karapatan.org/2018-Karapatan-HR-Report)]{.underline}.
History has shown that when the U.S. has made geopolitical calculations
at the expense of people's human rights, that has only [fomented
insecurity in the form of utter collapse]{.underline}. As the
[biggest](https://www.pgpf.org/chart-archive/0053_defense-comparison)
military power around the globe [by
far](https://www.pgpf.org/infographic/infographic-the-facts-about-us-defense-spending?),
the U.S. should prioritize stopping support to Duterte. An **[overblown
military presence in Asia Pacific only invites an arms]{.underline}**
**[race]{.underline}** **[with China.]{.underline}** We must stop
relying on militarization to ensure security. Last month, the San
Francisco Board of Supervisors
[condemned](https://balitangamerica.tv/san-francisco-supervisors-pass-resolution-condemning-dutertes-drug-war/)
Duterte's human rights abuses and called for a congressional hearing on
the U.S. funds fueling the violations, responding to the concerns of
Filipino residents in the Bay area. Other U.S. cities should do the
same. But most of all, in [solidarity](https://ichrpus.org/) with
movements for democracy, human rights, and social justice in the
Philippines, Congress must exercise its full powers of oversight to end
the military aid and arms sales to Duterte's regime.

#### US supported policies of Duterte's regime create human rights abuses and cause a chilling effect. 

**ICHRP '18** (The International Coalition for Human Rights in the
Philippines is a global network of organizations concerned about the
human rights situation in the Philippines and committed to campaign for
just and lasting peace. "Duterte Killings Continue: State Terror & Human
Rights in the Philippines" 2018.
<http://iboninternational.org/sites/ibon/files/resources/DKC-booklet.pdf>)
stowPCB

This collection of cases illustrates a [new wave of killings and human
rights abuses in the Philippines that is more expansive and insidious
than ever]{.underline}. The Filipino [people]{.underline}
[are]{.underline} once again [confronted]{.underline} [with]{.underline}
[state]{.underline} [terror]{.underline} [and]{.underline} the
[perils]{.underline} [of]{.underline} [fascist]{.underline} policies
[under]{.underline} the Rodrigo [Duterte]{.underline} presidency.
Reports and data that [human rights]{.underline} group Karapatan and
other [organizations]{.underline} [manage]{.underline} [to monitor do
not come close to the magnitude of individuals, groups and communities
victimized by the United States-backed Duterte regime and its police and
armed forces]{.underline}. Duterte's **[fascist policies are
increasing]{.underline}** -- from the counterinsurgency program Oplan
Kapayapaan, the merciless drug war campaign, the martial law in Mindanao
and the threat of expanding martial rule to the whole country, to
current moves toward authoritarian rule through charter change
ostensibly to shift to a federal system of government. The Duterte
government has also failed to disclose that [the US has launched in
September 2017 a new "counter-terror" operation called Pacific
Eagle-Philippines, which enables permanent US military presence that not
only violates the Philippine constitution, but also poses risk to
communities]{.underline}. This is in addition to onerous RP-US Visiting
Forces Agreement (VFA), which has [allowed]{.underline} rotational,
[permanent]{.underline} [presence]{.underline} [of]{.underline}
undisclosed [US troops]{.underline} in the country following its
ratification by the Philippine Senate in 1999. In the wake of these
policies are **[growing numbers of killings]{.underline}**, **[attacks
on communities, illegal arrests, harassments and other violation of
people's rights]{.underline}** especially with Duterte's cancellation of
the peace talks with the National Democratic Front of the Philippines
(NDFP). With Oplan Tokhang resulting in thousands of alleged drug users
or peddlers gunned down based on mere suspicion and police claims of
"nanlaban" (fought back), rights groups and people's organizations are
alarmed by [Duterte's order]{.underline} to shoot and kill suspected
armed rebels as this [gives state forces the license to kill unarmed
civilians]{.underline} expediently tagged as rebels. Furthermore, the
threat to crack down on activists and critics has a **[chilling
effect]{.underline}** on the public and the people's exercise of their
rights and liberties. Once again, Filipinos are faced by the truth that
rights are not granted by states, but must be always asserted and
defended. Clearly, the people must stand firm, raise their voices, and
collectively act against oppression and tyranny. **[The Duterte
government should be held accountable]{.underline}** for attacks against
the Filipino people, including thousands of victims of extrajudicial
killings perpetrated under the administration's campaign against illegal
drugs. As with the previous book series of IBON Foundation on State
Terror that disseminated information on the Arroyo government's crimes
against the Filipino people, this book aims to contribute in exposing
the Duterte regime's fascist and neoliberal economic policies and the
deteriorating human rights situation in the Philippines. Published by
the International Coalition for Human Rights in the Philippines and IBON
International, it hopes to stir international concern and solidarity and
galvanize greater action to resist continuing state violence and
tyranny.

### US Aid Bad

#### US aid worsens the humanitarian crisis in the Philippines. 

**Chew 19.** Amee Chew, Ph.D. in American Studies & Ethnicity, and is a
Mellon-ACLS Public Fellow. "It's Time to End U.S. Military Aid to the
Philippines" Foreign Policy in Focus. April 8, 2019.
<https://fpif.org/its-time-to-end-u-s-military-aid-to-the-philippines>.
EG.

Ever since the Philippines attained formal independence in 1946, the
U.S. has [maintained a military presence on its former colony, guiding
and supporting "counter-insurgency]{.underline}" operations to put down
constant rebellions against an oligarchic government. Today, the
[**Philippine armed forces** overwhelmingly direct violence not against
outside invaders, **but at poor and marginalized people within its
borders. U.S. military aid is only making internal conflict
worse**]{.underline}. **[U.S. taxpayer funds are bankrolling the
worsening human rights crisis in the Philippines.]{.underline}**
Duterte's repressive regime is
the¬†[largest](http://philippineslifestyle.com/military-aid-usa-philippines/)¬†[recipient](https://www.philstar.com/headlines/2018/09/10/1850124/philippines-largest-recipient-us-military-aid)¬†of
U.S.
military¬†[aid](https://explorer.usaid.gov/agencies/?agency=7&year=2017&measure=Obligations)
in East and SoutheastAsia. In 2016, the U.S. helped inaugurate Duterte's
drug war by giving [[\$32
million](http://www.philstar.com/headlines/2016/07/27/1607298/us-pledges-32m-philippine-law-enforcement)
to the Philippine police]{.underline} (supposedly for "[training and
services](http://www.rappler.com/nation/147196-us-funding-philippines-law-enforcement)"
in "policing standards" and "rule of law," besides
[equipment](https://oig.usaid.gov/sites/default/files/2018-11/lig-oco-opep-0918.pdf)).
In July 2018, the [United States announced an additional [\$26.5
million](https://ph.usembassy.gov/united-states-to-boost-counterterrorism-support-for-philippine-law-enforcement/)
in U.S. tax dollars to beef up support for Philippine police, in the
name of "counter-terrorism."]{.underline} In FY2018, the Defense
Department provided [[roughly \$100
million](https://oig.usaid.gov/sites/default/files/2019-02/OPEP_Q119_Dec2018_final.pdf)
in military aid,]{.underline} including equipment, weapons, and aerial
surveillance systems, to the Philippine military and police, though
Operation Pacific Eagle --- **[a so-called "overseas contingency
operation" that is [exempt](https://fas.org/sgp/crs/natsec/R44519.pdf)
from congressional limits on spending.]{.underline}** The amount
demanded for this program will increase to [\$108.2
million](https://oig.usaid.gov/sites/default/files/2019-02/OPEP_Q119_Dec2018_final.pdf)
for FY2019 --- even as the Defense Department has
[admitted](https://oig.usaid.gov/sites/default/files/2019-02/OPEP_Q119_Dec2018_final.pdf)
it lost track of transactions for 76 of 77 arms sales conducted under
bilateral agreements with the Philippines.

#### There are no restrictions on aid and a lack of transparency

**Chew 19**. Amee Chew, Ph.D. in American Studies & Ethnicity, and is a
Mellon-ACLS Public Fellow. "It's Time to End U.S. Military Aid to the
Philippines" Foreign Policy in Focus. April 8, 2019.
<https://fpif.org/its-time-to-end-u-s-military-aid-to-the-philippines>.
EG.

In 2018, on top of the above, the U.S. sold the Philippine
[police](https://oig.usaid.gov/sites/default/files/2019-02/OPEP_Q119_Dec2018_final.pdf)
and
[military](https://oig.usaid.gov/sites/default/files/2018-11/lig-oco-opep-0918.pdf)
over \$63 million worth of arms. It also donated [2,253 machine
guns](https://oig.usaid.gov/sites/default/files/2019-02/OPEP_Q119_Dec2018_final.pdf),
over [5
million](https://ph.usembassy.gov/us-government-provides-millions-of-rounds-of-ammunition-to-the-armed-forces-of-the-philippines/)
rounds of ammunition, surveillance equipment, and other weapons.
Military aid totaled at least \$193.5 million last year, not including
arms sales, and donated equipment of unreported worth. At least \$145.6
million is already pledged for 2019. In January, Trump authorized \$1.5
billion annually for the Asian Pacific region, including the
Philippines, from 2019 to 2023. Although this authorization includes a
[stipulation](https://www.congress.gov/bill/115th-congress/senate-bill/2736/text)
that counter-narcotics funds will not go to the Philippines ("except for
drug demand reduction," a potential loophole), it's too little, too
late**[. The set-aside has no restrictions on weapons funding for the
Philippine military]{.underline}**. And separately, the State Department
already plans to deliver [\$5.3
million](https://www.state.gov/documents/organization/290302.pdf) this
year to the Philippine police for anti-narcotics activities. **[Worse,
rampant corruption together with a total lack of transparency means it's
hard to ensure where military aid could actually end up.]{.underline}**
U.S. military equipment forms the backbone of Duterte's "military
modernization" program. Although the above aid is tiny compared to the
**[U.S.'s own bloated military budget, this tremendous transfer of
weapons and surveillance technology is significant in propping up the
Philippine armed forces' capacity.]{.underline}** Duterte has embarked
on an ambitious program to "modernize" the Philippine military,
[massively increasing funding and pouring more money towards this than
spent in [the last 15
years](https://www.philstar.com/opinion/2018/10/21/1861787/afp-budget-biggest-ever?fbclid=IwAR0KDcJItqxS3Cr1OstUNZRG-SXtaCzJ75rlLaRy0HQ1-pIAM7S46fYFiEQ).]{.underline}
(Meanwhile, he's
[doubled](https://news.abs-cbn.com/news/01/09/18/cops-soldiers-other-uniformed-personnel-to-begin-receiving-doubled-pay)
the salaries of military and police.) **[He could not do so without U.S.
aid and arms.]{.underline}**or its part, the U.S. is particularly
interested in
[expanding](https://oig.usaid.gov/sites/default/files/2019-02/OPEP_Q119_Dec2018_final.pdf)
aerial "intelligence, surveillance, and reconnaissance" missions over
Mindanao, the largest island in the Southern Philippines, rich in
untapped mineral resources. **[Without U.S. aid, the Philippine military
would lack the airplanes and technology to perform this
surveillance.]{.underline}**What's more, this year's Operation Pacific
Eagle budget sets aside an extra [\$3.5
million](https://oig.usaid.gov/sites/default/files/2019-02/OPEP_Q119_Dec2018_final.pdf)
for U.S. military efforts to collect and analyze "local media in native
languages" --- underscoring that the U.S. is striving for an upper hand
in directing Philippine military operations. And in winning an
information war over public opinion.

#### The US is complicit to the human rights crisis in the Philippines

**Chew 19**. Amee Chew, Ph.D. in American Studies & Ethnicity, and is a
Mellon-ACLS Public Fellow. "It's Time to End U.S. Military Aid to the
Philippines" Foreign Policy in Focus. April 8, 2019.
<https://fpif.org/its-time-to-end-u-s-military-aid-to-the-philippines>.
EG.

In recent years, the **[U.S. has had up to
[5,000](https://www.marinecorpstimes.com/news/your-marine-corps/2018/08/09/pentagon-triples-military-spending-in-philippines/)
troops deployed in the Philippines at any one time.]{.underline}**
Officially, U.S. troops are limited to "joint exercises" and war games.
But questions have been raised over **[[possible U.S.
personnel](https://www.manilatimes.net/us-soldier-among-dead/159838/)
involvement in secretive missions, resulting in killings of civilians
and human rights abuses.]{.underline}**In the case of the 2015
[Mamasapano](https://www.rappler.com/nation/82518-milf-fatalities-maguindanao-clash)
[massacre](https://newsinfo.inquirer.net/669237/moro-group-7-civilians-killed-3-wounded-in-mamasapano-clash#ixzz3QJi1rF9KF),
supposedly under the jurisdiction of Philippine police and military
only, hearings later
[uncovered](https://www.philstar.com/headlines/2015/03/17/1434648/senate-report-confirms-us-involvement-mamasapano-operation)
U.S. guidance and surveillance support, despite U.S.
[denials](https://www.mindanews.com/peace-process/2015/01/us-embassy-on-mamasapano-we-just-assisted-in-evacuation-of-dead-and-wounded/).
Meanwhile, U.S. troops who themselves commit human rights abuses,
murder, or [sexual
assault](https://books.google.com/books?id=u2HvCgAAQBAJ&lpg=PA90&ots=CIuNLhDOI3&dq=nicole%20subic%20bay%20settlement&pg=PA89#v=onepage&q=nicole%20subic%20bay%20settlement&f=false),
are insulated from being held accountable by the U.S.-Philippines
Visiting Forces Agreement.What are the consequences of the bonanza of
military aid for Duterte? **[The bottom line is, the U.S. government is
complicit in --- and actively supporting --- the deepening human rights
crisis in the Philippines.]{.underline}**[Police
are](https://www.amnesty.org.uk/files/2017-04/ASA3555172017ENGLISH.PDF?9_73DdFTpveG_iJgeK0U13KUVFHKSL_X)
[linked](https://www.bbc.com/news/world-asia-37172002) to the killings
carried out by unidentified vigilantes in the War on Drugs, and their
[corruption](https://www.hrw.org/sites/default/files/report_pdf/philippines0317_web_1.pdf)
[abounds](https://www.amnesty.org.uk/files/2017-04/ASA3555172017ENGLISH.PDF?9_73DdFTpveG_iJgeK0U13KUVFHKSL_X).
Besides **[tagging the unarmed people they have murdered as "fighting
back," police have
[planted](https://www.hrw.org/sites/default/files/report_pdf/philippines0317_web_1.pdf)
evidence;
[sexually](https://www.gmanetwork.com/news/news/nation/673124/center-for-women-s-resources-police-abuses-vs-women-involve-mostly-rape/story/)
[assaulted](https://globalvoices.org/2018/11/02/a-15-year-old-rape-victim-is-the-latest-collateral-damage-of-dutertes-drug-war/)
[women](https://www.gmanetwork.com/news/news/regions/646615/pregnant-mother-accuses-4-bulacan-cops-of-gang-rape/story/?fbclid=IwAR3tFeYU-dWI--I5TDv9ZBgukJmf0hYiSS1Js33ZYPbc632iQYJeu4ZuX64)
[and](https://ph.theasianparent.com/pregnant-woman-raped-by-police)
[children](https://www.philstar.com/nation/2018/10/29/1864004/cop-nabbed-rape-girl-15),
in
[exchange](http://nine.cnnphilippines.com/news/2018/11/08/pnp-charged-with-rape.html)
for release or dropping drug charges; and detained people without
charges and tortured them to extract bribes, including through the use
of
[secret](https://www.hrw.org/news/2017/04/27/philippine-drug-war-spawns-unlawful-secret-jail)
holding cells.]{.underline}**

### Solvency

#### Ending arms sales to the Philippines solves 

**Chew 19.** Amee Chew, Ph.D. in American Studies & Ethnicity, and is a
Mellon-ACLS Public Fellow. "It's Time to End U.S. Military Aid to the
Philippines" Foreign Policy in Focus. April 8, 2019.
<https://fpif.org/its-time-to-end-u-s-military-aid-to-the-philippines>.
EG.

**[The continuing drug war killings and rampant human rights abuses only
underscore that there is no way to ensure U.S. military aid to the
Duterte regime does not enable human rights violations.]{.underline}**
**[For its part, U.S. military spending is not only overblown, but also
often untraceable, secretive, and unaccountable.]{.underline}** From
Central America to Palestine to the Philippines, U.S. military aid has a
sordid legacy of fueling atrocities. **[A growing movement is calling on
Congress to cut military aid, arms gifts, and arm sales to the
Philippines --- as well as to end support for the Duterte
regime.]{.underline}** Congress **[must exercise its powers to ensure
the Leahy Law, which stipulates no funding shall be furnished to foreign
security forces if the U.S. knows they have committed "a gross violation
of human rights," is upheld with regard to the
Philippines]{.underline}**. (For more information on this campaign,
please visit: [ichrpus.org.](https://ichrpus.org)) In
[2007](https://www.govinfo.gov/content/pkg/CHRG-110shrg40811/html/CHRG-110shrg40811.htm),
due to movement pressure, Congress held a hearing on
[rising](https://www.thenation.com/article/how-us-aid-fosters-human-rights-violations-philippines/)
extrajudicial killings in the Philippines under Gloria Macapagal
Arroyo's regime. Legislation was passed placing restrictions on military
aid. The next year, killings decreased significantly

### Framing

#### Reject arms sales in the name of foreign policy goals -- geopolitical chess papers over violence against the most marginalized

**Miller 6-3** (Drew Elizard, The National Coordinator Of The U.S.
Chapter Of The International Coalition For Human Rights In The
Philippines., 6-3-2019, \"Congress: Stop Funding Duterte,\" Common
Dreams,
<https://www.commondreams.org/views/2019/06/03/congress-stop-funding-duterte)>
AG

- This card is about military aid, not arms sales -- not as helpful but
  still workable as a framework card

- Could read as solvency advocate?

Vega is right in his call for a congressional hearing on the
Philippines: [U.S. support has been **critical** to
[the](https://www.philstar.com/opinion/2018/10/21/1861787/afp-budget-biggest-ever)
[rise](https://news.abs-cbn.com/news/01/09/18/cops-soldiers-other-uniformed-personnel-to-begin-receiving-doubled-pay)
[of](http://cnnphilippines.com/news/2018/08/30/DND-Defense-proposed-budget-2019.html)
Duterte's military and police. Duterte's regime is the
[largest](http://philippineslifestyle.com/military-aid-usa-philippines/)]{.underline}

[aid](https://explorer.usaid.gov/agencies/?agency=7&year=2017&measure=Obligations)

for

and
[training](http://www.rappler.com/nation/147196-us-funding-philippines-law-enforcement)
in "policing standards" --- clearly detrimental when it comes to human

## Colonialism Adv

### History/Psych

#### The United States and the Philippines are connected by an enduring colonial relationship of exploitation -- withdrawal is key and prevents nuclear war.

**David, PhD, 89**(Leonard, [Revolutionary Struggle in the
Philippines]{.underline}, St. Martin's Press, p. 174-176)n

The first chapter in this book identified the [Philippines as a country
in crisis, political crisis, a country being **cramped into a right wing
perspective by the economic and military jaws of US aspirations for
world control,** and therefore]{.underline} world
[domination]{.underline}. In this global game, [the **Americans laugh
behind the backs of Filipinos** as they use and abuse them - providing
cheap labour to bring in huge profits for multinational
companies]{.underline}; [putting them in the front line in case of
nuclear attack;]{.underline} and having on hand an inexhaustible supply
of young Asian women to satisfy the insatiable sexual appetite of more
than 30000 service personnel who exploit and demean the inhabitants of
another sovereign country. [How does the \'moral majority\' in the US
square its conscience as 10 000 of its population go ashore each night
at Subic Bay]{.underline} - and others tumble out of the other bases -
**[to ravage the local population - women, men and even
children?]{.underline}** Conveniently, as it does in Western Europe,
[the US puts another country - in this case the Philippines - in the
\'hot seat\' for the first strike in the event of nuclear
war]{.underline}, perhaps [just hoping that one or two bombs \'would
bring the world to its senses\' and leave the US and its citizens
unscathed and unharmed. The **very presence of the US in the Philippines
increases the likelihood of nuclear war** with every day that
passes.]{.underline} In line with Emmanuel\'s analysis, reports in
Philippine Agenda show, for instance, that if a one-megaton bomb were
dropped on the JUSMAG offices in Quezon City - where extensive security
building works took place in 1987 - everything would be annihilated
within several miles. In an instant, 9000 people would be dead and most
buildings turned to rubble. Quezon City and San Juan residents would be
the most affected. Several seconds later, 1.25 million more would die
and hundreds of thousands of others would be severely injured in
surrounding municipalities (Sampaloc, Pandacan, San Miguel, Quiapo,
Santa Cruz, San Juan, dei Monte and parts of Paco, Santa Ana, Tondo,
Caloocan and Mandaluyong). Eighteen seconds after that, 750000 would die
in Makati, Ermita, Malate, Santa Ana, Paco, Intramuros, South Port, San
Nicolas, Binondo, Tondo, Navotas, Malabon, Marikina, Pasig and portions
of Valenzuela and Pasay. Forty seconds later, another 170000 people
would be dead in Paranaque, Pasay, Pateros, Taquig, Taytay, Cainta,
Antipolo, San Mateo, Obando, Meycauayan, and the rest of Malabon,
Novotas and Valenzuela. In less than aminute, over two million people
would have died and more would have been severelyinjured. Iffourofthe US
main facilities in the Philippines, namely, Clark Air Base, Subic Naval

Filipinos would die from the blasts, from burns, from radiation
sickness, and later from cancer. Many more would be severely hurt. Five,
10, 15 or 20 million Filipinos could perish as a result of thisor any
other reason - and **for many Americans this would only be yet another

dignity; women\'s bodies are something that Americans in the Philippines

the **exploitation, pollution and rape of the land bec;ome an
entitlement because of wealth and power.** If]{.underline} ever new
technology, [a]{.underline} new world order or the [opportunity for a
more desirable location for the siting of the bases could be found,
**the US would \'ditch\' the Philippines overnight.**]{.underline}
**[What does the word \'ally\' mean to the US?]{.underline}** When [more
than 3000 people drowned in the Philippines in the worst sea tragedy
known to man]{.underline} - on 20 December 1987 - [what relief did the
US send to families of the bereaved? **Nothing**]{.underline}. How
concerned was the US when such a sea disaster affected the lives of tens
of thousands of Filipinos? [What happened to the \'special
relationship\' so frequently referred to when antiAmerican feeling is
particularly apparent?]{.underline} Clearly, **[the most important thing
for the US to do is to pack up and leave.]{.underline}** [For 90 years,
they have used the Philippines as a staging post for aggressive acts

#### Colonial violence structurally influences the conditions of Filipinos leading to acculturative inferiority

**David & Nadal 13** \[E. J. R. David, psychology professor at the
University of Alaska Anchorage, Kevin L. Nadal professor at the John Jay
College of Criminal Justice - City University of New York, "The Colonial
Context of Filipino American Immigrants\' Psychological Experiences,"
*Cultural Diversity and Ethnic Minority Psychology*, 2013,
10.1037/a0032903\] // AT

The results of the two studies combine to suggest that [Filipino
American immigrants\' psychological experiences are **influenced by
colonialism and its legacies** while they were still in the Philippines
and after they arrive in the United States]{.underline}. Using
qualitative data. Study 1 **[findings provide initial empirical support
to the notion that ethnic and cultural denigration]{.underline}**---a
form of acculturative stress---are experienced by Filipino American
immigrants in the Philippines before they emigrated. Study 1 also
revealed that it is possible for [such experiences]{.underline} to
**[lead to the development of CM among Filipinos in the
Philippines]{.underline}**, that Filipino American immigrants may bring
such a condition with them when they move to the United States, and that
CM may influence the psychological experiences and mental health of
Filipino American immigrants. Using quantitative data from a national
sample of Filipino American immigrants. Study 2 findings support the
notion that **[the denigration of the Filipino ethnicity and culture in
the Philippines is common]{.underline}**. Messages about Filipino ethnic
and cultural inferiority were received from family members, peers, and
the general community, resulting in almost everyone in tbe sample being
socialized with, or at least exposed to, CM. [Study 2 also provides
evidence that such an exposure can lead to the intemalization of ethnic
and cultural inferiority, which is the initial stage and manifestation
of CM or intemalized oppression as observed from various
groups]{.underline} (David & Okazaki, 2006b; Fanon, 1965; Freir√©, 1970;
Memmi, 1965). Further, Study 2 results also provide evidence that CM
among Filipino American immigrants may be reinforced (or initiated) by
experiences of racism after arriving in the United States. [These
findings support the notion that Filipino]{.underline} American
[immigrants experienced acculturative stress]{.underline}---and thus
began their process of acculturation---[while they were still in the
Philippines, long before they immigrated to the United
States.]{.underline} 306 DAVID AND NADAL Table 2 Hierarchical Regression
of Status, Experiences of Racism, Race-Related Stress Appraisals, and
